Confessional Statement of Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11)	None
Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11), in his confessional statement has stated that the Appellant (A18) had been participating in smuggling activities with his consent, and that he had known what was being smuggled.	None
On 7th/8th February, 1993, he (A11) had gone to the house of Tiger Memon at the AlHusseini building in Mahim.	None
Tiger Memon had then taken him to the house of Anwar (AA), where they had met two other persons and he had learnt that the said people were Sayyed Abdul Rehman Shaikh (A28) and the Appellant (A18), and that the two had a tempo with them.	None
Tiger Memon had given him one lakh rupees and had asked him to go with the Appellant (A18) and to pay the said amount to Dawood Taklya (A14) and to return with a chemical i.e. black soap.	None
The said black soap was the same chemical that had been brought to the tower on the night of 3rd February, 1993.	None
He (A11) alongwith the Appellant (A18) and Sayyed Abdul Rehman Shaikh (A28) had left Mahim at midnight, and had reached the tower the next day at about 11 A.M.	None
An amount of rupees one lakh that had been given by Tiger Memon (AA), was handed over to Dawood Taklya (A14).	None
The Appellant (A18) along with Abdul Gani Ismial Turk (A11), and Sayyed Abdul Rehman Shaikh (A28) had then loaded about 59 bags of the said chemical into the tempo that evening, and had thereafter, left for Bombay.	None
They reached the Welcome Hotel at Panvel at about 1112 OClock at night.	None
They had met Tiger Memon (AA) there and he (A11) and the Appellant (A18) were directed to instruct Dawood Taklya (A14) to keep some persons ready for work.	None
They had conveyed the said message to Dawood Taklya (A14).	None
Dawood Taklya (A14) had sent his son Sarfaraz (A55) alongwith the Appellant (A18), Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11) and Sayyed Abdul Rehman Shaikh (A28) to Bombay.	None
Confessional Statement of Rusi Framroze Mulla (A125)	None
He has corroborated the prosecutions version of events regarding the transportation of smuggled goods from Shekhadi to Panvel.	None
Thus, in their confessional statements the aforesaid accused persons have revealed that the Appellant (A18) had fully participated in the landing and transportation of smuggled goods, which included weapons and not just silver and gold.	None
Confessional Statement of Parvez Nazir Ahmed Shaikh (A12)	None
He (A12) in his confessional statement has revealed that he had been working with Tiger Memon (AA) in the execution of hawala transactions and that he had been paying money to persons as was directed by Tiger Memon (AA) from time to time.	None
After the Bombay riots he could not attend the office of Tiger Memon (AA) as the same had been closed.	None
During this period he (A12), has stated that he, alongwith Ajgar were staying in Shaffis house and that he would call the house of Tiger Memons at the Al Husseini building intermittently, but upon his doing so, he was always told that there was no work.	None
Upon the instruction of Tiger Memon (AA) in January, 1993 he had gone to Mhasla and had met Dawood Taklya (A14) and had also participated in the landing.	None
The smuggled goods were brought from the jetty to the Wangni tower.	None
The men employed by Javed and Yakub who had come from Bombay had then opened the boxes which contained bullets, revolvers, pistols etc.	None
All the contraband were shifted into false cavities in the jeeps and tempos that had been organized, and which thereafter, departed for Bombay.	None
One such jeep had been entrusted to him (A12).	None
He along with Nasir had been told by Tiger Memon (AA) to wait at Khandala, and one contact number had been given to them.	None
At Khandala, they had gone to Hotel New Taj.	None
A12 had then tried to contact Tiger Memon (AA) over the telephone, using the said contact number at Hotel Big Splash, Alibagh.	None
However, he was only able to speak to Mohd.	None
Hussain who had advised A12 to wait there, and had stated that A18 would come there in the morning.	None
Consequently, the Appellant (A18) had come there with Imtiyaz in the afternoon.	None
With them, A12 had gone to Bombay, and had been dropped off at Bandra Talab and the Appellant (A18) and Imtiyaz had also left from there.	None
Confessional Statement of Sayyed Abdul Rehman Shaikh (A28)	None
His confessional statement reveals that on 5th February, 1993 at about midnight, when he (A28) was returning from shooting, the Appellant (A18) had met him on the road itself and had told him (A28) that Tiger Memon (AA) was calling for him.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) was standing nearby, and hence he met Tiger Memon who had told him to go to Mahim.	None
Yeda Yakub had also been standing there alongwith Tiger Memon.	None
Thus, he has corroborated the statement of Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11).	None
Confessional Statement of Liyakat Ali Habib Khan (A85)	Reasoning
His confessional statement reveals that in the second week of February 1993, his uncle Yakub Khan had asked his father to allow him to keep a few bags, for the period of a few months in their godown at Thane and thus, he had been allowed to do so.	None
After a while, his uncle Yakub Khan, Tiger Memon (AA) and Nisar had come to his house in a jeep and had taken him along with them.	None
After opening the godown of the factory, two tempos had been taken inside, and it was then that the goods were unloaded.	None
There were 80 packets in gunny bags, and each bag weighed about 30 to 35 Kgs.	None
Tiger Memon had given Liyakat Ali Habib Khan (A85) a sum of Rs. 600/ out of which he had given Rs. 200/ to Nisar and thereafter, Liyakat Ali Habib Khan (A85), Nisar and the Appellant (A18) had gone to the said factory and had then left for Bombay.	None
On the way, the Appellant (A18) had told him that the goods that had kept in their factory were actually explosives.	None
Sharif Abdul Gafoor Parkar Dadabhai (A17), in his confessional statement has disclosed that the Appellant (A18) had in fact been present when 59 packets had been brought into Bombay.	None
Deposition of Babydas Vasu (PW290)	None
He had been working in a hotel in Indraprastha at Nage Thana, District Raigad.	None
He has deposed that the Appellant (A18) alongwith others, had come there and had stayed in the said hotel for some time.	None
There are entries to this effect in the hand writing of the Appellant (A18).	None
Room No. 106 had been booked for them in the said hotel.	None
He has produced the register to prove the same, but the said entries are of the year 1992, and not of 1993.	None
Deposition of Pradeep S. Dalvi (PW293) He has deposed that he was the registered owner of the vehicle Matador Tempo bearing registration No. MMP4799 which had been sold to a decorator in 1988.	None
The said tempo, bearing this registration number had been used for the smuggling of various types of contraband, including weapons, from Shekhadi to Panvel by the Appellant (A18).	None
Deposition of Abdulmunaf A. Mahimi (PW294) He has deposed that he was the brother of Abdul Samad who had been carrying on the business of electrical and mandap decoration, and that the said vehicle had been purchased by his brother Abdul Samad (not examined) between 5.2.1993 and 9.2.1993.	None
The tempo was not found in the campus.	None
The said vehicle had been seized on 30.11.1993, but no samples etc. were taken from the vehicle to determine whether it contained RDX explosives etc. or not.	None
Deposition of Asit Ghorai (PW602)	None
He has deposed as a panch witness and has stated that 13 samples were in fact taken after the seizure of the vehicle on 30.11.1993.	None
The samples were then sent for chemical analysis.	None
Deposition of Ajit Surve (PW604)	None
He has proved the seizure of the vehicle and the sending of the RDX samples for chemical analysis and also the receipt of the report stating that RDX had been found therein.	None
Deposition of Moreshwar Thakur (PW469)	None
He has deposed that the Test Identification Parade had been held in accordance with law, and has further stated that some witnesses had identified the Appellant (A18), as the person who was had been involved in the landing at Shekhadi.	None
After due consideration of the entire evidence on record, the Designated Court came to the conclusion that as the Appellant (A18) was involved in the Shekhadi landings operation, he has committed the offence u s 3(3) TADA.	None
The evidence has also established his involvement in commission of the offence of conspiracy with the object of committing terrorist acts, as the Appellant (A18) had been made aware of the nature of the smuggled goods and had still transported the same.	None
The said act amounts to furthering the object of conspiracy to commit terrorist acts.	None
However it has been held that the Appellant (A18) himself has not committed any act and that he himself has not participated in any conspiratorial meetings, to denote that he was actually a party to the conspiracy to commit serial bomb Blast or a party to the larger conspiracy i.e. the first charge.	None
So far as the Appellant (A18) is concerned, undoubtedly, there is sufficient evidence to show that he was involved in the transportation of contraband.	None
From the facts and circumstances of the case, and after taking into consideration the evidence on record, it cannot be inferred that despite being a close associate of Tiger Memon (AA), he remained unaware of the nature of the contraband.	None
Furthermore, when a person has been transporting goods for a long period of time it is difficult to believe that he would transport the said goods, without ascertaining the exact nature of goods being loaded into his vehicle, particularly, in view of the fact that the vehicle is likely to be checked at several places by the police, as well as by custom officials.	None
Thus, we do not see any cogent reason to hold that the Appellant (A18) is not guilty of the charges for which he has been punished by the Designated Court.	None
II.	Issue
Sayyed Abdul Rehman Shaikh (A28)	Issue
The Appellant (A28) has been convicted on two counts u s 3(3) TADA for the offence of conspiracy, and has been awarded 7 years rigorous imprisonment alongwith a fine of Rs. 25,000/, and in default of payment of fine, to suffer further RI for 6 months on each count.	Issue
In addition to the first charge of conspiracy, he had been charged u s 3(3) TADA for the following offences That he participated alongwith the other coaccused in the landing and transportation of arms, ammunition and explosives at Shekhadi, and transported the same from Shekhadi, Mhasla to Shilphata, Bombay in a Motor Tempo, bearing Registration No. MCY2279.	Issue
Further, he (A28) has also transported RDX explosives from Mhasla to the godown of coaccused Noor Mohmed Haji Mohmed Khan and Mohmed Jindran Mumtaz Jindran in Motor Tempo No. MMP4799, while accompanied by Shakil Shahbuddin Shaikh (A59).	Issue
He (A28) has been convicted and sentenced as mentioned hereinabove.	Issue
Ms. Farhana Shah, learned Counsel for the Appellant has submitted that the Appellant (A28) did not own the van in which the goods were transported.	Arguments of Petitioner
Moreover, he has served 3 years out of the total sentence awarded to him, and is now 60 years old.	Arguments of Petitioner
Therefore, leniency should be shown to him.	Arguments of Petitioner
Thus, the appeal deserves to be allowed.	Arguments of Petitioner
146.	Arguments of Petitioner
Shri Mukul Gupta, learned Senior Counsel appearing for the State has submitted that he was involved in the transportation of arms and ammunition within the territory of India, and owing to the serious nature of the offence committed by him, there should be no leniency.	Arguments of Respondent
Thus, the appeal deserves to be dismissed.	Decision
We have heard learned Counsel for the parties and perused the record.	None
Evidence against the Appellant (A28) Confessional statement of the Appellant (A28) Confessional statement of Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11) Confessional statement of Dawood Taklya Mohammed Phanse (A14)	None
Confessional statement of Sharif Parkar Dadabhai (A17)	None
Confessional statement of Suleman Mohammed Kasam Ghavate (A18) Confessional statement of Shakil Shahbuddin Shaikh (A59) Confessional statement of Shahnawaz Khan (A128) Deposition of Vijay Govind More (PW. 137) Deposition of Uttam K. Kale (PW. 190) Deposition of Dileep M. Katarmal (PW. 284)	None
Confessional statement of Sayyed Abdul Rehman Shaikh (A28)	None
His statement was recorded by Sanjay Pandey (PW. 492), DCP on 23.4.1993 and 26.4.1993.	None
In his confessional statement, he has disclosed that he was a driver by profession and that he had a driving licence.	None
He had known Tiger Memon (AA) for the last 67 months and also Anwar, Gani (A11), Rafique Madi and Haji Yakub.	None
Hazi Yakub was a friend of Anwars.	None
He had gone to Ajmer alongwith the other coaccused Suleman and Anwar in April 1992, for smuggling activities.	None
After 23 months of his visit to Ajmer, upon the instructions of Anwar, the Appellant (A28) had reached Bandra station with one change of clothes.	None
Shafi and Suleman had come there in a Maruti car, in which he (A28) had also driven alongwith them, till Linking Road.	None
From there, the Appellant (A28) alongwith the others had gone to an open theatre by way of taking a jeep.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) had arrived there alongwith Imtiyaz and Anwar in a blue coloured Maruti car.	None
Anwar had instructed the Appellant (A28) to follow the car of Tiger Memon (AA), and they had gone to Panvel and had reached the Welcome Hotel.	None
Anwar had gone with Tiger Memon (AA).	None
Imtiyaz and the Appellant (A28) were directed to reach the tower alongwith the other coaccused.	None
They had gone to Goregaon, Raigad and had slept there at night.	None
At about 3.30 in the morning, Tiger Memon (AA) had come with a truck carrying Imtiyaz, Anwar, Dadabhai (A17), Dawoodbhai (A14) and about 2025 labourers.	None
The Appellant (A28) had woken up and realized that there were also two more jeeps and one truck.	None
Silver bricks were removed from the truck that had been brought by Tiger Memon and the same were loaded into all the vehicles standing at the tower.	None
The Appellant (A28) alongwith Rafique Madi, had taken 18 silver bricks and had thereafter, proceeded towards Hyderabad.	None
In Kolhapur, they had handed over the goods to Pradeep Chandra Jain and had thereafter, returned to Bombay with an empty vehicle.	None
After this, on 5.2.1993 at about 12.30 A.M., when he was returning from shooting (as he has claimed that he worked in movies, particularly in stunts), he had been called by Tiger Memon (AA), and had been asked to go to Mhasla.	None
Yeda Yakub who was also there, had given him the keys to a Matador tempo, which belonged to Abdul Samad, a decorator in Mahim.	None
He had gone to Mhasla alongwith Suleman (A18) and Gani (A11) and there he had met Dawood Bhai who had taken them near the tower, and had told them that the goods had been kept in a pit, and that it would take some time to remove them.	None
Dawood (A14) had then asked him, alongwith the others to return at around 77.30 a.m. with a vehicle.	None
From there he had gone to the house of a lady (school teacher) in Mhasla Village, and had eaten and also rested there.	None
In the evening, they had gone to the tower.	None
It was a moonlit night, and at the said time Dawood (A14) and Dadabhai (A17), alongwith their 1015 servants had come there and had proceeded to load the goods, i.e. 5560 sacks into the vehicle that had been brought by him.	None
Some empty sacks were also put in after folding the same over the goods.	None
They had then gone to the Welcome Hotel at Panvel.	None
Tiger Memon had also come there.	None
Tiger Memon had sent Gani (A11) and Suleman (A18) to the Persian Darbar Hotel.	None
Then Tiger Memon had gone inside the Welcome Hotel with the Appellant (A28), they had met one fair and tall person who had brown eyes.	None
The Appellant (A28) had been introduced to him by Tiger Memon (AA), and was also directed to work in accordance with his instructions.	None
On being asked, the Appellant (A28) had disclosed that he (A28) had also seen the Delhi Darbar Hotel in Dahisar Check Naka.	None
Then, the fair tall man had told the Appellant (A28) to park the said vehicle in front of the hotel, on the other side of the road and had told him that one Shakeel (A59) would meet him there, who would then unload the vehicle.	None
As per the instructions of Shakeel, the Appellant (A28) had proceeded to park the vehicle.	None
A Nepali had then come there, and some persons had unloaded the goods from the vehicle and had then brought the said vehicle back to the Delhi Darbar Hotel, after which, the Appellant (A28) had left for Virar in the said vehicle.	None
Subsequently on 8.2.1993, at about 66.30 in the evening, Anwar had met the Appellant (A28) at Bandra Talab naka and had asked him to go to Mhasla again.	None
The Appellant (A28) had gone there alongwith Yakub.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) had also arrived there after about one hour alongwith a jeep.	None
He had given the jeep to Suleman (A18) and thereafter, told him to leave.	None
The Appellant (A28) upon the instructions of Tiger Memon (AA), had returned alongwith the vehicle and had handed over the said vehicle to Gani (A11) and returned to Bandra Talab.	None
Anwar had then paid Rs. 5,000/ to the Appellant (A28) in the evening, in lieu of the aforementioned job.	None
The Appellant (A28) had thus been working continuously for Tiger Memon.	None
However, he had been unaware of the contents or nature of the goods.	None
It was only after the Bombay Blast had taken place on 12.3.1993, and when Tiger Memons name had appeared in the newspapers, that the Appellant (A28) had realised that he had committed a mistake by participating in the said landing and transportation, as he thought that perhaps, instead of silver and gold, it had actually been weapons that were smuggled in by him.	None
He was arrested during the shooting of a movie, in which he was working.	None
Confessional Statement of Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11)	None
His confessional statement has revealed that the Appellant (A28) had been at the residence of Tiger Memon (AA) at the AlHusseini building.	None
When he had gone there on 4.2.1993, after about 45 days, he had met Suleman Kasam Ghavate (A18) and Sayyed Abdul Rehman (A28).	None
They also had a tempo with them.	None
Tiger had given Gani (A11) a sum of Rs. 1 lakh and had asked him to go alongwith the Appellant (A28) and Suleman Mohammed Kasam Ghavte (A18), to pay the said amount to Dawood Taklya (A14), and while returning, to bring back with them, the black soap.	None
It was the same black soap which had been brought to the tower on the night of 3.2.1993.	None
The tempo was thus loaded by the Appellant (A28), alongwith Suleman Mohammed Kasam Ghavte (A18) and several others.	None
The same finally contained 59 boxes of chemical, and was brought to Bombay, after which he had met Tiger Memon.	None
Confessional Statement of Dawood Taklya Mohammed Phanse (A14)	None
In his confession, he has revealed that after collecting the smuggled goods, he alongwith others, including the Appellant (A28) had reached the tower.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) had instructed all the persons to remain outside, except his own men.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) had even asked the watchman (A62) to leave.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) had further instructed them to remove all the empty boxes and jute cloth from there, and to burn the same.	None
At the time when they had gone inside, they had seen that the men of Tiger were opening boxes, and that they were placing rifles, pistols, bullets, hand grenades, bundles of wire with white pencils on top of them, and black soap like material on the side.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) was seen sitting on the side and after counting, he would make notes in his diary.	None
Baba, Driver (A73) and the Appellant (A28), were among the men of Tiger Memon who were opening the cavities of the jeeps and tempos parked there.	None
At this time, Tiger Memon (AA) took out a pencil like thing made of white steel like material, and showed the same to him (A14) and to Dadabhai (A17).	None
He had told them that each object was worth Rs. 25,000/ and that the same could even be used to explode the Oberoi Hotel.	None
Confessional Statement of Sharif Parkar Dadabhai (A17)	None
His confessional statement has disclosed that on 7.2.1993 Gani (A11) had come with a tempo.	None
He had been accompanied by Miya Suleman Ghavte (A18) and Sayyed Abdul Rehman Shaikh (A28).	None
At this time, Gani (A11) had brought Rs. 1 lakh with him and had given the same to Dawood Taklya (A14).	None
The smuggled goods were loaded into the tempo, which then left for Bombay.	None
Confessional statement of Suleman Mohammed Kasam Ghavate (A18)	None
This accused (A18) in his confessional statement disclosed that he reached Mhasla on 6.2.1993 alongwith Appellant (A28) and A11, A14 and A17 were already present there.	None
They put 5963 packets containing powder in a vehicle.	None
While they were coming back they met Tiger Memonn (AA) in Panvel.	None
On 8th February, 1993, A18 drove a white tempo as directed by Anwar and got off at Panvel.	None
After some time, another yellow tempo, driven by Appellant (A28) arrived there in which A18 sat and drove upto Mahad.	None
They reached in front of Besawa Hotel in Mahad where another tempo, driven by Appellant A28 appeared and then they went to Mhasla where goods were divided in both the tempos.	None
On their way to Panvel, he saw Tiger Memon (AA) in a car and he asked A18 to take the tempo to Chilparakalyan.	None
When they reached Chilparakalyan, they met Tiger Memon (AA).	None
Tiger Memon drove the tempo himself and came back with an empty tempo in half an hour.	None
Shakil Shahbuddin Shaikh (A59) and Shahnawaz Khan S o. Faiz Mohmed Khan (A128) in their confessional statements have supported the case of the prosecution, as they have stated that the Appellant (A28) had participated in the landing and transportation.	None
Deposition of Uttam K. Kale (PW. 190)  	None
He deposed that he has recorded the confession of Appellant (A28).	None
On 1.6.1993, Appellant (A28) expressed his willingness to make a voluntary confession because of repentance and denied being induced or coerced.	None
He was given 48 hours to rethink and he recorded his statement on 4.6.1993 as he was busy on 3.6.1993.	None
The said witness identified the confessional statement of A28 in court.	None
Deposition of Vijay Govind More (PW. 137)  	None
He deposed that he was working as labourer at Wangni Tower.	None
He wrongly identified the Appellant (A28) as Anwar and in his statement did not name Appellant (A28) but corroborated in general particulars in respect of transportation of goods smuggled at Shekhadi.	None
He also stated that goods were unloaded at Wangni Tower and shifted in another vehicle and at that time Tiger Memon (AA) and Dawood Taklya (A14) among others were present.	None
Dileep M. Katarmal (PW. 284) in his statement has deposed that A17 has purchased a few dozens gunny bags from his shop on 10.2.1993, though he did not name the Appellant (A28)	None
specifically but he corroborated in general particulars the confession of Appellant (A28) wherein he stated that he alongwith Najeeb had purchased 1500 sacks from the said shop.	None
Considering the material contained in the confession of the Appellant (A28), and in those of the aforesaid coaccused, it was held that the same leads to the inescapable conclusion that the Appellant (A28) had infact been involved in the Shekhadi landing operation, and had thus committed the offence u s 3(3) TADA.	None
The evidence also establishes his involvement in the commission of the offence of conspiracy to commit terrorist acts since the Appellant (A28) was certainly aware of the nature of the contraband material, and had still transported the same, the said act amounts to furthering the object of the conspiracy to commit terrorist acts.	None
However, it was held that the Appellant (A28) had not committed any acts and had not participated in any conspiratorial meetings, to denote that he had been a party to the conspiracy to commit the serial bomb Blast or the larger conspiracy i.e. the first charge.	None
So far as the Appellant (A28) is concerned, his confessional statement which stands corroborated by the confessional statements of the other coaccused, particularly, Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11), Dawood Dawood Taklya (A14), Imtiyaz Yunusmiya Ghavte (A15), Sharif Abdul Gafoor Parkar Dadabhai (A17) and Shahnawaz Khan (A128) reveals his involvement in the Shekhadi landing and further establishes that he had been fully aware of the nature of contents of the contraband and had still transported the same.	None
Such an act tantamounts to furthering the object of the conspiracy to commit terrorist acts.	None
Taking into consideration his close association with Tiger Memon (AA) and his associates, with respect to their smuggling activities, it is difficult to believe that he was unaware of the nature of the contents.	None
Thus, we are of the view that he has rightly been convicted u s 3(3) TADA by the Designated Court.	None
III.	Facts
Sajjad Alam Iqbal Abdul Hakim Nazir (A61)	Issue
The Appellant (A61) has been convicted u s 3(3) TADA on two counts, and has been awarded 7 years rigorous imprisonment alongwith a fine of Rs. 50,000/, and in default of payment of fine, to suffer suitable RI.	Issue
The Appellant (A61) has been charged for criminal conspiracy, and in addition thereto, has also been charged u s 3(3) for his participation in the landing at Shekhadi on 3rd and 7th February, 1993 and in the transportation of arms, ammunition, hand grenades and explosives like RDX which were to be used in the Bombay Blast on 12.3.1993, and further, for using his auto rickshaw bearing registration	Issue
No. MH062243 to bring the aforementioned smuggled items to Bombay.	Issue
He has been acquitted of the first charge of conspiracy, however, he has been convicted of the second charge u s 3(3), and has been sentenced as referred to hereinabove.	Issue
Ms. Farhana Shah, learned Counsel for the Appellant has submitted that his confession had not been made voluntarily, and that the same had been retracted on 3.12.93 and therefore, must not be taken into consideration.	Arguments of Petitioner
Hence, the appeal deserves to be allowed.	Arguments of Petitioner
163.	Arguments of Petitioner
Shri Mukul Gupta, learned Senior Counsel for the Respondent, has submitted that even if the confessional statement of the Appellant (A61) was retracted, the same has been corroborated by the confessional statements of the other coaccused, as well as by the depositions of various witnesses.	Arguments of Respondent
Therefore, this appeal deserves to be dismissed.	Decision
We have considered the rival submissions made by learned Counsel for the parties and perused the record.	Reasoning
Evidence against the Appellant (A61) Confessional statement of the Appellant (A61) Confessional statement of Dawood Taklya (A14) Confessional statement of Khalil Ahmed Sayed Ali Nasir (A42) Confessional statement of Imtiyaz Yunusmiya Ghavte (A15) Confessional statement of Muzammil Umar Kadri (A25)	None
Confessional statement of Tulsiram Dhondu Surve (A62) Deposition of Vijay Govind More (PW137) Depositions of Chandrakant Afaraz (PW111), Vyankatesh Hirba (PW588) and Shridhar Gawade (PW151).	None
Confessional Statement of Sajjad Alam Iqbal Abdul Hakim Nazir (A61)	Reasoning
His own confession has been recorded by Shri K.L. Bishnoi, DCP (PW. 193), wherein he has revealed that he had taken certain persons in his auto rickshaw bearing No. MH062243, to the place of the landing.	None
He had seen that certain materials had been removed in gunny bags from a jeep i.e. 16 rifles and 32 cassettes and that the same were taken into a room where the Appellant (A.61) was not allowed to enter.	None
He had been paid Rs. 4,000/ for participating in two landings.	None
He has further revealed that on 9.2.1993 Dawood Taklya (A14) had met him at the Mhasla S.T. Stop and had asked him to come to Mehandari.	None
He (A61) had taken him to Mehandari where they met Khalil Nazir and Muzammil (A25).	None
Here, Dawood had told Muzammil to hand over to him 3 rifles and 6 cassettes.	None
Muzammil had then handed over the said weapons in gunny bags.	None
The Appellant (A61), Khalil and Dawood Taklya (A14) had gone alongwith the said arms, to Lonery Phata.	None
After sometime Tiger Memon (AA) had arrived there in his blue Maruti car and thereafter, the said goods were shifted to his car.	None
Confessional Statement of Dawood Taklya (A14)	None
He has disclosed that on the date of the landing, Tiger Memon (AA) had sent him to the place of landing alongwith some persons who had also been given guns by Tiger Memon (AA).	None
Such armed persons were spread over all sides.	None
After sometime the said goods had arrived in a trawler.	None
Persons who had been called from the village then began to unload these goods and bringing them to shore.	None
Khalil and Iqbal (A61) had also come there with trucks.	None
The entire cargo was loaded into two trucks and thereafter, they all come to T.V. Tower, where the said goods were unloaded.	None
Some time after this, Tiger had instructed them to remove all the empty boxes and jute bags from there and to burn the same.	None
When they had gone inside, they had seen the men of Tiger opening boxes which contained rifles, pistols, bullets, hand grenades, black soap and bundles of wires with white pencils on top.	None
Confessional Statement of Khalil Ahmed Sayed Ali Nasir (A42)	Reasoning
His statement has disclosed that the aforementioned goods were smuggled.	None
He had gone to the house of Dawood Taklya (A14) in the afternoon at about 4 p.m. to inform him that the landing of the said goods would take place that night, and that Appellant (A61) should thus be sent to Dawood Taklya at 7 p.m. by Rickshaw.	None
On the said day he had sent Appellant (A61) from Mehandari to Mhasla in his Rickshaw.	None

After due consideration of the entire evidence on record, the Designated Court came to the conclusion that the Appellant (A61) being involved in the Shekhadi landing operation, has committed the offence u s 3(3) TADA.	None

None
The Appellant (A61) had also received an amount of Rs. 4000/ for the work done by him in the landing operation.	None
The evidence on record clearly establishes the above and thus, the fact that he was one of the main persons who was responsible for effecting the said landing.	None
Hence, he has rightly been convicted by the learned Special Judge u s 3(3) TADA, and no interference is required in the said order.	None

We have heard learned Counsel for the parties and perused the record.	None

The confession of the Appellant (A73) was recorded by Shri Vinod Balwant Lokhande, D.C., Airport Zone, Bombay on 15.5.1993 and 17.5.1993.	None
In his confessional statement, the Appellant (A73) has disclosed that he has been working in the garage of his maternal uncle since his childhood.	None
His uncle had handed over the garage to him 27 years ago.	None
He had been running the said garage for repairing vehicles.	None
He knew Tiger Memon (AA) and his associates Sunil, Shaffi, Imtiyaz, Anwar, Rafique Madi, Raju Marwari, Riyaz, Majeed etc.	None
They would do the work of smuggling silver.	None
The same was unloaded at the seashore near the village Mhasla.	None
The goods were to be brought by trucks to the Tower, and the contraband were then to be unloaded and concealed in the cavities of tempos and jeeps there.	None
The work of the Appellant (A73) was to take the tempo or the jeep full of smuggled silver to its destination, and after this, he was paid a sum of Rs. 2,000 to 3,000 for each transportation landing.	None
In the last week of January, 1993 he had reached the Welcome Hotel, Panvel alongwith the jeep at 8.30 p.m. upon receiving instructions to this effect.	None
Four jeeps and a Maruti car were already parked there.	None
Tiger and Sunil were also sitting in the jeep.	None

The truck was then unloaded, and all goods were kept in the tempos and jeeps.	None

The Appellant (A73) had parked the tempo full of smuggled goods outside his garage in Islampura.	None

The Appellant (A73) was asked by Tiger Memon to take the tempo outside his garage to Sankhvi street, opposite Bata Company, near Lokhandi gate near the place where Chiliyaki Hotel was situated.	None
He was informed that there would be a boy at the gate who would give him a signal with a white handkerchief upon seeing the said tempo.	None
The Appellant (A73) was told to take the vehicle as per his direction, and unload the goods there.	None
The next day, the Appellant (A73) had taken the tempo to Sankhvi Street to the aforesaid address, and as per the direction, the goods were unloaded there.	None
He had been paid Rs. 1000 for this work.	None
The Appellant (A73) has confessed that he had participated in landings of silver, and that it was only on one occasion that weapons had been smuggled.	None

Rafiq (A46) have supported the case of the prosecution by stating that the Appellant (A73) participated in the landing and transportation of the smuggled goods including arms, ammunition etc.	None

In his confessional statement, he has disclosed details of the incident dated 28th/29th February, 1993.	None
He has stated that at 1.302.00 a.m., the smuggled goods had been were brought in a lorry to the tower, and that Tiger Memon (AA), Yakub (AA), Javed (AA), Dawood Taklya (A14) and their men and Ors. had also come there.	None

Deposition of Vinod Lokhande (PW. 183)	None
He has recorded the confessional statement of the Appellant and he deposed that it was voluntary and had been made strictly in accordance with law and the confessional statement was forwarded to the Chief Judicial Magistrate, Alibagh.	None
In view of the above, we have to consider whether in light of the evidence on record, the conviction of the Appellants can be sustained.	Issue
All the material on evidence was collected and after appraisal, the Special Judge came to the conclusion that A73 had in fact been involved in the landing operations of the contraband substances.	None
The evidence against Appellant (A73) includes his own confession wherein he has confessed to being fully aware of the fact that the contraband were shifted from trucks to other vehicles, which contained arms, ammunition and RDX.	None
The Designated Court came to the conclusion that his act of driving the vehicle containing such material could not be for any purpose other than to aid and abet terrorist activities.	None
However, the Designated Court has stated that the said acts had been committed by him in the early phases of the conspiracy, even prior to Tiger Memon (AA) deciding the target of the Blast.	None
The court also went on to say that after this particular incident A73 had not been involved in any landing job.	None
Therefore, he (A73) cannot be held guilty for the larger conspiracy, for which the charge firstly, was framed against him.	None
So far as Appellant (A73) is concerned, like other Appellants, his involvement and participation in the landing operations of the contraband substances has been clearly established.	None
His own confessional statement has revealed that he, being fully aware of the contents of the contraband, shifted the same from the truck to other vehicles and that in spite of the fact that he knew that the contraband contained arms, ammunition and RDX, he continued to be associated with the other coaccused.	None
Therefore, he has aided and abetted terrorist activities, and we do not see any cogent reason to interfere with his order of conviction as recorded by the Designated Court.	None
In view of the above, we do not find any substance in these appeals and the same stand dismissed.	Decision

Decision
This appeal has been preferred against the judgment and order dated 2.8.2007 passed by Special Judge of the Designated Court under the TADA for Bombay Blast Case No. 1 of 1993, by which the Respondent has been convicted u s 3(3) TADA, and awarded rigorous imprisonment for 7 years alongwith a fine of Rs. 25,000/, and in default of payment of fine, to suffer further RI for six months, and secondly RI for 7 years u s 3(3) TADA, but had been acquitted of the charge of larger conspiracy.	Issue
Hence, this appeal.	Facts
Heard rival submissions by counsel for both parties and perused the evidence on record.	Reasoning
The evidence against the said Respondent includes his own confession wherein he had disclosed that he was a driver and was acquainted with Tiger Memon (AA), Mohd.	None
Rafiq (A46), Anwar (AA), Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11), Suleman Mohd.	None
Kasam Ghavate (A18) and Uttam Potdar (A30).	None
In April 1992, the accused (A28) had gone along with Suleman Mohd.	None
Kasam Ghavate (A18) and Uttam Potdar (A30) to Ajmer for taking silver.	None
On 5.2.1993 Suleman Mohd.	None
Kasam Ghavate (A18) took the accused (A28) to Tiger Memon (AA) who asked him to go to Mhasla.	None
Yeda Yakub gave the accused (A28) the keys of a tempo in which the accused (A28) alongwith Suleman Mohd.	None
Kasam Ghavate (A18) and Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11) went to Mhasla.	None
On the next day, at Mhasla the accused (A28) met Dawood Taklya (A14) who took him alongwith other coaccused to Wangni Tower and told them that the goods are to be dug out from a pit.	None
After the goods were taken out, they were placed in the vehicle in the presence of Dawood Taklya (A14).	None
Then, they came to Nagothane (near Pen) and stayed in a hotel.	None
The accused (A28) alongwith Tiger Memon (AA) went inside Welcome Hotel wherein they met a man who told the accused (A28) to park the vehicle in front of Hotel Delhi Darbar at Dahisar Check naka.	None
The accused (A28) parked the vehicle as directed and the goods were unloaded there with the help of some persons.	None
The accused (A28) again met Tiger Memon (AA) on 8.2.1993 and went to Mhasla alongwith Anwar and Tiger Memon and brought 1500 sacks from one Gujarati in Pen.	None
On 11.2.1993 Tiger Memon met them at Goa Road and asked Suleman Mohd.	None
Kasam Ghavate (A18) and the accused (A28) to accompany him till Kalyan, wherein they handed over the vehicle to Tigers man, namely, Usman Gani Choudhary.	None
The accused (A28) was paid Rs. 5,000/ for the said job.	None
The said confessional statement was duly supported and corroborated by the confessional statements of Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11), Dawood Taklya (A14), Suleman Mohd.	None
Kasam Ghavate (A18) and Uttam Potdar (A30), Sharif Abdul Gafoor Parkar (A17) and Shakil Shabbuddin Shaikh (A59).	None
Uttam M. Kale (PW. 190) also supported the prosecutions case to the extent that the confessional statement was given by the accused (A28) voluntarily and it had been recorded strictly in accordance with law.	None
The deposition of Sanjay Pandey (PW. 492) and Vijay Govind More (PW. 137) also supported the case of the prosecution.	None
After appreciating the evidence on record the learned Designated Court recorded the conclusion as under Thus in light of the reasoning given aforesaid, it will be difficult to accept submission of Ld.	None
Chief P.P. to give maximum punishment to A18 28 for the reasons canvassed by him and dealt earlier and so also for any other reason, which is also precisely absent.	None
At the cost of repetition, it will be necessary to say that even it is accepted that smuggling of arms, ammunition and explosives substance, even accepted to be very heinous merely on said count awarding maximum punishment to each of the accused involved in such landings de hors considering the extent of act committed by him and thereby assessing the element of criminality exist in him would amount allowing oneself to be swayed by feeling and would amount of having acted without any logical reasoning behind it.	None
Having regard to the same while awarding punishment to A18 28 it will be necessary to take into account the gravity of the act committed by both of them and so also the other circumstances relevant to same as urged on their behalf or even otherwise.	None
The parameters laid down by this Court in entertaining the appeal against the order of acquittal have to be applied.	Reasoning
The instant case is similar as that of Suleman Mohd.	None
Kasam Ghavate (A18) and therefore, we are not in a position to take a view different to the view taken in that case.	None
The appeal lacks merit and is accordingly dismissed.	Decision
This appeal has been preferred against the judgment and order dated 2.8.2007 passed by Special Judge of the Designated Court under the TADA for Bombay Blast Case No. 1 of 1993, by which the Respondent has been convicted u s 3(3) TADA and awarded rigorous imprisonment for 8 years with a fine of Rs. 10,000/ and in default of payment of fine, to suffer further RI for 2 months on the first count and on second count he has been awarded u s 3(3) TADA, a rigorous imprisonment for 6 years with a fine of Rs. 5,000/ and in default of payment of fine, to suffer further RI for one month.	Issue
In addition to the general charge of conspiracy the Respondent (A73) was charged for participating alongwith his coconspirators in the smuggling and landing of arms and ammunition at Shekhadi and participating in transportation of the same from Shekhadi to Bombay for committing terrorist activities.	Facts
He was further charged under the provisions of Arms Act for possessing storing the weapons at his garage and unauthorisedly transporting smuggled weapons from Shekhadi to Bombay.	Facts
After conclusion of the trial, the Respondent had been convicted u s 3(3) TADA, but had been acquitted of the first charge of conspiracy.	Facts
Hence, this appeal.	Facts
Heard rival submissions made by counsel for both parties and perused the evidence on record.	Reasoning
The learned Special Judge after considering the evidence on record against the Respondent recorded the following findings 61C)	None
Thus considering material in the confession of A73 and aforesaid coaccused the same leads to the conclusion of A73 also being involved in Shekadi landing operations denoted by said material and as such having committed offence u s 3(3) of TADA for which he is charged at head 2ndly.	None
Similarly, considering said evidence in proper perspective and same and particularly own confession of A73 squarely denoting that he was fully aware that contraband goods which were shifted from trucks to other vehicles where arms, ammunition, handgrenades and RDX etc.	None
and still himself having transported the same to Bombay by driving vehicle and even in Bombay having committed further acts regarding contraband goods the same clearly indicates that his act were directed to further object of conspiracy to commit terrorist act.	None
No doubt that he has received amount of Rs. 1 thousand for work effected by him.	None
However the same will never change character of act committed by him.	None
Similarly the acts committed by him were obviously for purposes of aiding and abetting terrorist accused who were to use the same for commission of terrorist act.	None
A73 having committed said act by contravening provision of Arms and Explosive Act he was also required to be held liable for offence u s 6 of TADA for which he charged at head 3rdly.	None
However unlike other accused involved in transportation alike A73, A73 after Shekhadi landing operation had not participated in commission of any act furthering object of any conspiracy.	None
The acts were committed by him during early phase i.e. much prior to even Tiger Memon fixing target for commission of serial blast.	None
A73 had never been party to any conspiratorial meeting after effecting said landing job nor was involved in any of operation thereafter effected in pursuance of conspiracy to commit serial blast.	None
In view of same though A73 is found to be guilty for offence of conspiracy the same would be conspiracy to commit terrorist act punishable u s 3(3) of TADA or in other words he cannot be held liable for larger conspiracy for which charge at head 1stly is framed against him.	None
In view of the fact that there is no evidence to show that the Respondent (A73) ever participated in any of the conspiratorial meetings after the said landing, or was involved in any of the operation thereafter in pursuance of the conspiracy to commit the serial Blast, he could be punished only for smaller conspiracy u s 3(3) TADA and not for the larger conspiracy for which the charge No. 1 had been framed.	None
In the facts and circumstances of the case, the Respondent (A73) had been convicted and awarded sufficient punishment.	None
The parameters laid down by this Court in entertaining the appeal against the order of acquittal have to be applied.	Reasoning
In view of the above, we do not find any cogent reason to hold that findings recorded by the learned Designated Court are perverse, warranting any interference by this Court.	Decision
The appeal lacks merit and is accordingly dismissed.	Decision
This appeal has been preferred against the judgment and order dated 2.8.2007 passed by the Special Judge of the Designated Court under the TADA for Bombay Blast Case No. 1 of 1993 by which the Respondent has been convicted u s 3(3) TADA on two counts and awarded rigorous imprisonment for 7 years with a fine of Rs. 25,000/ and in default of payment of fine, to suffer further RI for a period of six months on one count and 7 years rigorous imprisonment u s 3(3) TADA on the second count.	Issue
However, he had been acquitted of the first charge of conspiracy.	Facts
The appeal has basically been filed only for enhancement of punishment, or for conviction of the Respondent for main charge of conspiracy.	Facts
In addition to the first charge, the general charge of conspiracy had been framed for participating in the landing and transportation of contraband at Shekhadi for commission of terrorist activities for transporting the smuggled contraband, including weapons through his tempo bearing No. MMP4799 from Shekhadi to Panvel for committing terrorist acts and further for participating in weapons training at Shekhadi.	Facts
Out of the said charges, the charge of participation in weapons training at Shekhadi was not proved.	Facts
Hence, this appeal.	Facts
Heard rival submissions made by the counsel for both parties and perused the evidence on record.	Reasoning
The evidence against the said Respondent has been his own confession which had been retracted and it had been corroborated by the confessional statements of Abdul Gani Ismail Turk (A11), Parvez Nazir Ahmed Shaikh (A12), Sayyed Abdul Rehman Shaikh (A28), Liyakat Ali Habib Khan and Sharif Abdul Gafoor Parkar (A17).	Arguments of Petitioner
His involvement in the crime has also been corroborated by the deposition of Uttam M. Kale (PW. 190) in whose presence the confessional statement of coaccused had been recorded.	None
Deposition of Vijay Govind More (PW. 137), a labourer at Wangni Tower and Sanjay Pandey (PW. 492) have also supported the case of the prosecution.	None
The Designated Court appreciated the evidence and held as under Thus, considering material in the confession of A18 and aforesaid coaccused the same leads to the conclusion of A18 also being involved in Shekhadi landing operation as denoted by said material and as such having committed offence u s 3(3) of TADA for which he is charged at head 2ndly clauses a and b to the extent of transportation of contraband material of the said landing effected by him.	None
Similarly, considering the manner in which he had acted in the said episode for furthering the object of conspiracy to commit terrorist act as denoted by said material the same also establishes his involvement in commission of offence of conspiracy to commit terrorist act punishable u s 3(3) of TADA.	None
Now taking up work of determining sentence for A18 28 in light of submission canvassed at Bar, reasoning given during earlier part of judgment and particularly declaration made in consequent to same on 11th of October, 2006 regarding A18 and 17th Oct., 2006 regarding A28 reveals that though both of them were charged for commission of offence of conspiracy and for commission of offence u s 3(3) of TADA i.e. A18 on 3 subcounts A28 on 2 subcounts each of them was found guilty for commission of offence only on two subcounts to the extent as found during the assessment of evidence for commission of offences punishable u s 3(3) of TADA.	None
Without unnecessarily reiterating every aspect connected with decision arrived accordingly, in short it can be said that both of them are found guilty accordingly mainly due to acts committed by each of them in connection with Shekhadi Landings and or transportation of contraband goods smuggled by effecting the said landings.	None
The said landing was effected by Tiger Memon on two occasions in month of February, 1993 in which Tiger Memon and his associates at the behest of absconding accused Dawood Ibrahim has smuggled arms, ammunition and explosives and transported same from Shekhadi Coast via Wangni Tower to Bombay.	None
The evidence surfaced and or reasoning given thereon earlier also reveal that both A18 28 since earlier had close association with Tiger Memon and were carrying out the work of Drivers for transportation of smuggled goods and in the questioned landing they had transported the contraband goods in a manner as discussed in the earlier part of the judgment.	None
The reasons given earlier in terms reveal the evidence having established that both of them were men of confidence of Tiger Memon.	None
The same also reveals that they were aware and or had become aware about the nature of the goods which they were transporting and or had transported.	None
Having regard to the same and having regard to the fact that both of them, even after acquiring the knowledge had not taken any steps revealing that they were against transportation of such a contraband goods, which was arms and ammunition and RDX material and since the act committed by them being in the nature of furthering the object of conspiracy to commit terrorists act, they were held guilty for the offence of a conspiracy to the said extent.	None
Since, evidence has not revealed that both these accused had committed any further acts after the said transportation and or thereafter A18 having stopped the work for Anwar at the behest of whom he was involved in the said work and so also both of them being not connected with any of the operation effected for achieving the object of entire conspiracy i.e. both of them being not involved in acquiring the training, attending conspiratorial meetings, in which the targets were selected etc.	None
they could not be held guilty for commission of offence of conspiracy to commit the serial bomb blast etc.	None
The parameters laid down by this Court in entertaining the appeal against the order of acquittal have to be applied.	Reasoning
We do not see any cogent reason to interfere with the impugned judgment.	Decision
The appeal lacks merit and is accordingly dismissed.	Decision
This appeal has been preferred against the judgment and order dated 2.8.2007 passed by Special Judge of the Designated Court under the TADA for Bombay Blast case, Greater Bombay in B.B.C. No. 1 of 1993.	Issue
The Respondent Tulsi Ram Dondu Surve (A62), has been found guilty for offences punishable u s 3(3) TADA, and on the said count, has been convicted and sentenced to suffer RI for 9 years and a fine of Rs.	Issue
50,000/ and in default, to suffer further RI for one year.	Issue
He has also been found guilty u s 202 Indian Penal Code, and sentenced to suffer RI for 6 months and ordered to pay a fine of Rs. 5,000/, and in default of payment of fine, he was ordered to suffer further RI for one month.	Issue
Both the sentences were directed to run concurrently.	Facts
However, he has been acquitted for charge of conspiracy.	Facts
Hence, this appeal.	Facts
Shri Mukul Gupta, learned Senior Counsel appearing for the Appellant would submit that the Respondent (A62) was a Watchmana government servant, at Wangni Tower.	Arguments of Petitioner
He had not only facilitated the unloading of goods smuggled in India, rather served the smugglers by taking money as a consideration for this work.	Arguments of Petitioner
He was fully aware of the contraband material but he did not inform the police authorities about the same.	Arguments of Petitioner
Therefore, he ought to have been held guilty of the charge of conspiracy also.	Arguments of Petitioner
226.	Arguments of Petitioner
On the contrary, Ms. Farhana Shah, learned Counsel appearing for the Respondent has opposed the appeal contending that he has already served 5 years of sentence.	Arguments of Respondent
He did not participate in hatching the conspiracy by attending any conspiratorial meetings.	Arguments of Respondent
Therefore, this Court should not grant any indulgence, taking into consideration the parameters laid down by this Court for hearing the appeal against order of acquittal.	Arguments of Respondent
The appeal is liable to be dismissed.	Arguments of Respondent
We have considered the rival submissions made by learned Counsel for the parties and perused the record.	Reasoning
Evidence against Respondent Confessional statement of Respondent (A62) Confessional statement of Dawood Phanse (A14) Confessional statement of Sharif Abdul Gafoor Parkar (A17) Deposition of Usman (PW. 2) Confessional statement of Respondent Tulsi Ram Dondu Surve (A62)	Arguments of Petitioner
In his confessional statement, the Respondent revealed that he was working as a Watchman in Wangni Tower.	None
Dawood Phanse (A14) had become acquainted with him and Tiger Memon (AA) who had been using Wangni Tower for loading, unloading and shifting the contraband from one vehicle to another.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) used to keep the smuggled goods and silver in Wangni Tower.	None
As Harish Chandra Surve (PW. 108) and Vijay Govind More (PW. 137) had also been working in the same tower as employees, the Respondent had persuaded them for helping the smugglers.	None
Payment was made to them from the money received by him for rendering such assistance.	None
He also disclosed that Dawood Phanse (A14) had purchased 10 acres of land in the name of the accusedRespondent (A62).	None
In respect of the incident of smuggling, he disclosed that one tempo, jeep and Maruti car arrived at the Wangni Tower.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) and his associates Iqbal, Mobin, Anwar, Munna, Shafi were accompanying the vehicles.	None
Silver bricks were shifted from the truck into the tempo.	None
There were gunny bags and boxes covered with clothes also and about 50 bags out of the aforesaid goods remained unloaded.	None
The said bags were taken by the truck of Alware in the field which was in his name and were concealed in the pits by putting soil on it.	None
Dawood Phanse (A14) had told him that the contraband was Kala Sabun, and he was warned not to disclose the same to any one.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) cut one bundle from the said bundles, and saw the same to ascertain whether the goods were proper or not.	None
He threw the plastic at that place and packed the same in another bundle and took the same with him.	None

One truck, three jeeps, one rickshaw and two motor cycles came there alongwith the accused persons, namely, Dawood Phanse (A14), Dadamiya Parkar (A17), Sharif Adhikari (A60), Abdul Gharatkar (A34) and Tiger Memon (AA).	None
After 56 days Dawood Phanse (A14) had paid him Rs. 2,000/ for the assistance.	None
Dawood Phanse (A14) used to give an amount of Rs. 1000/ for each of them i.e. accused, Harish Chandra Surve (PW. 108) and Vijay Govind More (PW. 137).	None
Confessional statement of Dawood Phanse (A14)	None

Same remained the position in respect of the confessional statement of Sharif Abdul Gafoor Parkar (A17).	None
Even the Deposition of Usman (PW. 2) corroborated the same.	None
After appreciating the entire evidence, the Designated Court came to the conclusion as under 59AThe aforesaid material contained in the confession of A62 not only reveals his involvement in Shekadi landing transportation but also reveals involvement of A14, 17, 27, 34, 42, 55, 60, PW 108, PW 137 and Tiger Memon.	None
59BThe corroborative material to matters contained in confession of A62 i.e. his involvement in Shekadi landing transportation operation for which he is charged with is also found in the confession of coaccused No. 17.	None
59CThus considering material in the confession of A62 and aforesaid coaccused the same leads to the conclusion of A62 also being involved in Shekadi landing operation as denoted by said material and as such having committed offence u s 3(3) of TADA for which he is charged at head 2ndly clause a and b.	None
Similarly the same evidence also establishes his involvement in commission of offences for which charge was framed at head 3rdly i.e. offence u s 202 of Indian Penal Code on count of himself in spite of being watchman and Government servant has still knowingly and intentionally omitted to give information about offences committed in his presence being in possession of contraband material unauthorisedly.	None
The parameters laid down by this Court in entertaining the appeal against the order of acquittal have to be applied.	Reasoning
We have given our conscious thought to the facts but are not convinced that the Respondent can be held guilty for the charge of larger conspiracy also.	Decision
We concur with the learned Special Judge so far as the Respondent is concerned.	Decision
The appeal lacks merit and is dismissed accordingly.	Decision
This appeal has been preferred against the judgment and order dated 2.8.2007 passed by Special Judge of the Designated Court under the TADA for Bombay Blast Case No. 1 of 1993 by which the Respondent (A61) had been convicted u s 3(3) TADA and awarded rigorous imprisonment for 7 years with a fine of Rs.	Facts
50,000/.	Issue
However, Respondent (A61) has been acquitted of the general charge of conspiracy.	Issue
Hence, this appeal.	Facts
Shri Mukul Gupta, learned Senior Counsel appearing for the Appellant, has submitted that the Respondent had very close association with terrorists and had been a kingpin in all the terrorist activities and most of the accused in their confessional statements had revealed his involvement.	Arguments of Petitioner
Therefore, he ought to have been convicted for the charge of general conspiracy and, thus, the appeal deserves to be allowed.	Arguments of Petitioner
237.	Arguments of Petitioner
On the contrary, Ms. Farhana Shah, learned Counsel appearing for the Respondent, has submitted that the Respondent (A61) has already been convicted and punished appropriately.	Arguments of Respondent
He has already served 31/2 years in prison and had paid fine, therefore, no further punishment is required and the appeal is liable to be dismissed.	Arguments of Respondent
The evidence against the Respondent Sujjad Alam Iqbal Abdul Hakim Nazir (A61) is his own confession.	None

Accused (A61) participated in the landing and transportation of the contraband.	None
Accused (A61) was paid Rs. 2000/ per landing through Khalil.	None
On 20th January, 1993, Accused (A61) went to the residence of his maternal uncle and found Khalil, Muzammil, Shafi and other Khalil, resident of Shrivardhan present there.	None
They were shifting some goods wrapped in gunny bags from the jeep to a room.	None
At that time, son of Dawood Taklya Sarfaraz (A55) was also there.	None
Shafi, driver of Tiger Memon (AA), asked accused (A61) to leave the room.	None
When they opened the gunny bags inside the room, accused (A61) saw that the bags contained 16 rifles and 32 cassettes (magazines).	None
After coming outside, A61 saw that Khalil, resident of Shrivardhan, was closing secret cavities in the jeep.	None
Shafi then took that jeep towards Mhasla.	None
The accused (A61), Khalil and Muzammil took the said arms, ammunition in the auto rickshaw of Muzammil at the residence of Muzammil and dropped the same there.	None
On 3rd February, 1993, his uncle Khalil asked him to help in the landing of contraband for Tiger Memon (AA) in the night.	None
So A61 went to the place of landing in his auto rickshaw alongwith Dawood Taklya (A14) and Abdul Aziz.	None
After reaching there, he found 23 jeeps carrying Tiger Memon (AA) and 2025 of his associates.	None
The accused (A61) was then directed to reach Tower, upon which, he left to wake the people there.	None
On reaching the place the accused (A61) parked the vehicle on one side of the tower and slept on the back seat.	None
After a long time, Muzammil came to the vehicle and woke him up.	None
Rashid and Khalil also came there.	None
By that time, all the vehicles from Shekhadi had arrived.	None
The associates of Tiger Memon (AA) were unloading and shifting the articles inside the Tower.	None
The accused (A61) was forbidden to enter inside.	None
After sometime, Dawood, Khalil, Abdul Aziz and accused (A61) left the Tower in the auto rickshaw.	None
It was in the evening of 9th February, 1993, that the accused (A61) took Dawood Taklya in his auto rickshaw to Mehandari.	None
From there they took Khalil Nazir from his residence and reached Muzammils residence.	None
On being asked by Dawood Taklya, Muzammil handed over 3 rifles and 6 cassettes in a gunny bag.	None
All the three accused then took the said weapons and ammunition and came to Lonery Phatta on the highway via Goregaon and handed over the same to Tiger Memon (AA), who had arrived there.	None
After 45 days, Dawood Taklya sent Rs. 4000/ for both the landings.	None
Confessional statement of Mohd.	Reasoning
Phanse Dawood Taklya (A14)  	None
His statement corroborated the version given by the accused (A61) about the landing at Shekhadi and disclosed the role of accused (A61) as a participant in the landing and his facilitation in the transportation.	None
According to him, Tiger Memon (AA) was there with 2025 persons.	None
Out of them 810 persons were carrying pistols in their pockets.	None
Immediately, after the arrival of trawler, accused (A61) was sent alongwith his auto rickshaw to call Rashid from Borli with his truck so he left.	None
The goods were unloaded and put in the trucks.	None
Immediately, another trawler arrived carrying the goods which were also unloaded.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) made 23 boys carrying guns to sit over the goods which were loaded in the truck.	None
Then they had reached Wangni Tower, where the goods were unloaded.	None
When they went inside the Tower, he saw the men of Tiger Memon (AA) opening those boxes and putting rifles, pistols, bullets, black wire, handgrenades and bundles of wire with white pencil on top and black soap like material at the side.	None
Tiger Memon (AA) was sitting at their side and counting and noting things in his diary.	None
Once the landing and transportation was over, coaccused (A14) came back to his village alongwith accused (A61) in his auto rickshaw.	None
Confession of Khalil Ahmed Sayed Ali Nasir (A42)  	None
So far as accused (A61) is concerned, A42 in his confessional statement disclosed that on 3rd March, 1993 he and Dawood Taklya (A14) had reached Mhasla in the autorickshaw of accused (A61).	None
Then the accused (A61) was sent to village Borli with autorickshaw to bring the truck and labourers.	None
Confession of Muzammil Umar Kadri (A25)  	Reasoning
On 3rd February, 1993, this accused (A25) on being called reached in front of Bashirs house in Borli.	None
Accused (A61) auto rickshawala also came there sometime later after dropping Dawood Taklya (A14) and Khalil at Shekhadi.	None
Sometime later, Khalil had come alongwith another Khalil of Shrivardhan on his scooter.	None
Khalil sent accused (A61) to the tower just before the jeep came and accused (A25) also went to the tower alongwith Khalil by following the truck.	None
On 7th February, 1993, Dawood Taklya (A14) had taken him in the auto rickshaw of accused (A61), to Shekhadi.	None
In the morning of 7th February, 1993 Dawood Taklya (A14) had come in the rickshaw of accused (A61) and took 3 rifles and 6 cassettes which had been kept in his house earlier.	None
The remaining 13 rifles and 26 cassettes had been recovered later on by the police from his house.	None
Deposition of Vijay Govind More (PW. 137)  	None
This witness deposed about the incident of February, 1993 stating that Tiger Memon (AA) and his companions came in jeeps and motorcycles and an auto rickshaw at Wangni Tower.	None
Accused (A61) was also with them.	None
He also identified the accused (A61) in court.	None
The Designated Court after appreciating the entire evidence reached the conclusion as under The aforesaid material contained in the confession of A61 not only reveals his involvement in Shekadi landing and transportation but also reveals involvement of A14, 15, 17, 25, 27, 34, 42, 55 Tiger Memon.	None
In addition, the Designated Court also reached the conclusion that the accused (A61) had no knowledge about the use to which weapons were to be put into.	None
In awarding the punishment, the court took into consideration the role played by the Respondent (A61) and concluded that charge for larger conspiracy could not be made out.	None
It is evident that he was not allowed to enter into the Wangni tower and thus he had no knowledge that arms had been smuggled into India to be used in Bombay Blast, and further, the fact that the arms were kept in the house of Muzammil, and the arms and ammunition had been transported in the vehicle belonging to Muzammil and not in the vehicle of accused (A61).	None
There is nothing on record to show that accused (A61) had participated in loading and unloading of the same.	None
His rickshaw had been used for carrying the accused persons.	None
The accused (A61) had transported the arms, i.e. 3 rifles and 6 cassettes alongwith Dawood Taklya from the house of Muzammil which were subsequently taken from him by Tiger Memon (AA).	None
The scope and ambit of Section 3(3) TADA is very wide.	None
Punishment for the offences u s 3(3) varies from 5 years to life imprisonment depending on the gravity of the overt act done by particular accused.	None
Each of them cannot be held to be at par, as one of them may be instrumental in arranging the landing, another maybe helping in organising and affecting transportation, some may be given supervisory work while other persons might have been engaged as labourers.	None
Therefore, while determining the quantum of punishment the precise act committed by an individual accused is of prime consideration.	None
In the instant case, Appellant (A61) had been found guilty on the single count of participating in landing on two occasions and additionally of being involved in the concealment of arms and ammunition at the house of A25 and further for the transportation of some arms from the house of A25 to Lonery Phata and handing over the same to Tiger Memon (AA).	None
Undoubtedly he had been working as an auto driver and was paid only for that.	None
The parameters laid down by this Court in entertaining the appeal against the order of acquittal have to be applied.	Reasoning
The judgment of the learned Special Judge does not require interference.	Facts
The appeal lacks merit and is accordingly dismissed.	Decision
Criminal Appeal No. 512 of 2008 This appeal has been preferred against the judgments and orders dated 21.5.2007 and 25.5.2007, passed by the Special Judge of the Designated Court under the TADA in Bombay Blast Case No. 1/93, Greater Bombay, by which the Appellants have been convicted Under Sections 3(3) and 6 TADA.	Issue
In view of the fact that each Appellant being assigned different acts, has been charged differently and has been awarded a different sentence, it is desirable to deal with the case of each Appellant separately to certain extent.	Issue
Abdulla Ibrahim Surti (A66) Appellant (A66) was charged for concealing 12 AK 56 rifles, 36 magazines and 19500 cartridges of AK 56 rifles which were kept in 3 bags in a cloth and 13 cloth bags were kept in the mango grove of Abdul Razak Subedar.	Issue
These arms and ammunition had been smuggled into India to be used for terrorist activities and were recovered at his instance on 7.4.1993 from the said place.	Facts
He was further charged for disposal of the said arms and ammunition alongwith other coaccused dumping the same in Kandalgaon creek.	Issue
and lastly for aiding and abetting the coaccused Shabir (AA) and Jamir (A133) having possession and carrying fire arms and ammunition u s 6 TADA.	Issue
Appellant (A66) stood acquitted on the first charge of conspiracy.	Issue
However, he has been convicted Under Sections 3 (3) TADA and awarded RI of five years and a fine of Rs. 25,000/, and in default of payment of fine, to suffer further RI of six months.	Facts
u s 6, has been awarded RI of six years and a fine of Rs. 25,000/ and a suitable R.I. for default of payment of fine.	Facts
Hence, this appeal.	Facts
Ms. Farhana Shah, learned Counsel appearing for the Appellant (A66) has stated that the Appellant (A66) had no knowledge that the items being transported were arms and ammunition.	Arguments of Petitioner
Moreover, he has not made any confession and the confessional statement of the coaccused cannot be relied upon to convict him.	Arguments of Petitioner
Further it was urged that he (A66) has already served 3 years out of the sentence that has been awarded to him.	Arguments of Petitioner
Thus, the appeal deserves to be allowed.	Arguments of Petitioner
253.	Arguments of Petitioner

5,000/. On 9th January, 1993, he was again contacted by Uttam Potdar (A30) and he went for landing alongwith Firoz Khan, Mechanic Chacha (A136) and Shabbir Kadri.	None

Faki Ali Faki Ahmed Subedar (A74) Appellant (A74) was further charged for concealing 12 AK 56 rifles, 36 magazines and 19500 cartridges of AK 56 rifles which were kept in 3 bags in a cloth and 13 cloth bags in the mango grove of Abdul Razak Subedar.	Issue

Issue
After conclusion of the trial, Appellant (A81) stood convicted and sentenced to suffer RI for 6 years and a fine of Rs. 50,000/, and a suitable R.I. for default of payment of fine u s 3(3) TADA and further sentenced to suffer RI for 3 years and a fine of Rs.	Facts
25,000/ for conviction u s 111 read with Section 135(b) of the Customs Act, 1962.	Facts

There are further depositions of Janu Vethkoli (PW. 378), T.S. Bhal (PW. 191), Shridhar Borkar (PW. 88), Dattatray (PW. 89), Anil Baswat (PW. 90) and Ashok (PW. 670) to support the allegations against the present Appellant A81.	None
Deposition of Tikaram Shrawan Bhal (PW191)	None
He has recorded the confessional statement of Gambas (A81) as well as the confession of Faki Ali Faki Ahmed Subedar (A74).	None
He had deposed that he had recorded the same strictly in accordance with law, and it was a voluntary confessional statement and after recording the same he had given time to rethink as required in law, and after recording the confession, the same was forwarded to CJM, Alibagh on 21.5.1993.	None
The issue whether confessional statements made by Faki Ali Faki Ahmed Subedar (A74) and Janardhan Pandurang Gambas (A81) were voluntary, had been considered by the Designated Court in its judgment and after considering all the objections it came to the conclusion that Faki Ali Faki Ahmed Subedar (A74) and Janardhan Pandurang Gambas (A81) had made confessional statement voluntarily as T.S. Bhal (PW. 191), S.P., Raigad has deposed that the Appellant (A81) was produced by Ashok Krishanji Chandgude (PW. 670) before him on 20.5.1993 and after asking certain questions to him, T.S. Bhal (PW. 191) was fully satisfied that Appellant (A81) wanted to make a voluntary confession.	None
He was again asked to be produced on 21.5.1993 and on that day Appellant (A81) narrated the entire matter and his confession has been recorded verbatim.	None
The Designated Court rejected the suggestion in his (A81) Section 313 Code of Criminal Procedure statement before the court that he had never been produced before T.S. Bhal (PW. 191) on either of the two days as claimed by the prosecution and his thumb impression had been obtained on blank papers while he was in custody of Alibagh Police Station.	None
The theory was rejected.	None
After appreciating the evidence on record the learned Designated Court came to the conclusion that the involvement of the Appellant (A81) in landing at Dighi Jetty is established, but there is hardly any evidence to reveal that the Appellant (A81) had knowledge of contraband goods being arms and ammunitions, and thus the Appellant (A81) cannot be held liable for offence u s 3(3) TADA on said count i.e. first limb of second charge, but guilty for offence punishable u s 111 read with Section 135(b) of Customs Act, 1962 for the same.	None
However it was held that the Appellant (A81) after having acquired the knowledge about nature of said contraband being arms and ammunition and still having committed acts mentioned in second and third limbs of second charge i.e. concealment of weapons in mango groves and dumping of cartridges and magazines in Khandalgaon creek, he would be guilty for commission of offence u s 3(3) TADA for the said offences.	None
More so, the Designated Court has taken into consideration the other confessional statements of other accused to support the prosecution case.	None
We are not inclined to interfere with the judgment of the Designated court.	Decision
The appeal with reference to Gambas (A81) lacks merit and is accordingly dismissed.	Decision

(Ext. 2650).	None

The same not being rebutted by the Appellant (A104) would lead to conclusion of him being in possession of contraband material and liable for commission of offence u s 3(3) TADA i.e. second limb of second charge.	None
